
   Message Format
  ----------------

   Message #1 of 8250 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

   <Subject>

   <1 blank separator line>

   <Date/Time>

   <Person & email address>

   <2 blank separator lines then...>

   <Message - "As-Is">

   <2 blank lines then @'s as divider line>


   * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
     Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
     is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
     view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
     Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
     "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

     Thanks to Mark de Jong (from the AMOS-LIST) for helping me with rebuilding
     Floquet's ASCII signiture. (who else would keep emails for 7 years?!)

     Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
     me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

     Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
     the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
     addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.


   Message From Archivist
  ------------------------

   I hope everyone enjoys reading the messages and appreciates me archiving
   them. It took hours of work to get all the info into this file and then 
   rebuild the ASCII signitures as best as I could.
   Don't forget to join, or atleast visit, the Y! AMOS-LIST group:

     http://groups.yahoo.com/group/amos-list


          - Andrew D. Burton, February 2008
            aliensrcooluk@yahoo.co.uk

	Message #2056 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: 2 questions,,,,

Sat Jan 2, 1999 2:34 am
Rune Zedeler <rune@zedeler.dk>


On 01-Jan-99, Cori Skagen wrote:
>From: Cori Skagen <lskagen@ssm.ca>

>1. Can I load a font directly without having to always load the font list
>from disk?

You can fool amos (slam-solution) - and I know it's very ugly:

Procedure _SETFONT[NEWFONT$,SIZE$]
OLDDIR$=Dir$
Dir$="Fonts:"
OLDFONT$=Dir$
Dir$=OLDDIR$
Exec "c:copy fonts:"+NEWFONT$+".font T: quiet"
Exec "c:makedir T:"+NEWFONT$
Exec "c:copy fonts:"+NEWFONT$+"/"+SIZE$+" T:"+NEWFONT$+"/ quiet"
Assign "Fonts:" To "T:"
Get Fonts
Repeat
Inc FONT
F$=Font$(FONT)
Until Left$(F$,Len(NEWFONT$))=NEWFONT$ and Mid$(F$,31,Len(SIZE$))=SIZE$
Set Font FONT
Exec "c:delete T:"+NEWFONT$+".font quiet"
Exec "c:delete T:"+NEWFONT$+"/ all quiet"
Assign "Fonts:" to OLDFONT$
End Proc

This is something I just wrote. I haven't tried it - something does probably
not work. But you can try it.

>2. Can I redimension an array?

I don't think so.
But perhaps you can place your main program in a procedure. And every time you
need to redim an array you quit the proc and call it again...
(Dim the array inside the proc, then) ...

Nah...

This lib sent out is a beta...it isn't complete. I pointed this out ;o)

The only gfx commands that do anything to TGE screens are tge gfx commands. So
normal amos commands won't do a thing to a tge screen. In the first non-beta
realease (if you all give PAC enough support to continue the project), there
will hopefully be a tge version of all the amos gfx commands. Even bobs.

Why not come up with some nice demos using the plot command, it really is very
fast. Along with the line drawing commands. (check out the manual)

	Message #2061 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

TGE - first impression

Sat Jan 2, 1999 9:39 pm
Rune Zedeler <rune@zedeler.dk>


I just took a look at the ß-version.

It is not at all AMOS implemented. This means that AMOS will simply be put to
back when a Gamescreen is opened - and AMOS' own mouse-, joy-, and
keyboard-functions will hence not work.
Everytime you open or close a Screen, the Workbench will become visible for a
short moment.
It is not possible to display more than one screen at the time.
As far as I could see, you could not in any way get to some of the nice
AGA-functions like dual playfield, copper rainbows, dual palettes, etc...

All in all you sort of feel like you are working on a damn pc when it comes to
gfx.

Sorry, but I'll keep working on my AGA-extension.

Re: TGE - first impression

Sat Jan 2, 1999 6:13 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 03-Jan-99, Rune Zedeler wrote:
>From: Rune Zedeler <rune@zedeler.dk>

>I just took a look at the ß-version.

>It is not at all AMOS implemented. This means that AMOS will simply be put to
>back when a Gamescreen is opened

what did you expect to happen ?

AMOS does not give the extension programmer any access whatsoever to its
database,
to change where to write gfx to or anything like that.

>It is not possible to display more than one screen at the time.

Thats because of grahpics cards, they dont have a copper.

>As far as I could see, you could not in any way get to some of the nice
>AGA-functions like dual playfield, copper rainbows, dual palettes, etc...

well, 50% of amiga users have AGA, the rest are still on ECS or RTG at this
stage, and loads more are still getting gfxcards, espically the bvision. So
if I had made it be AGA only then 50% of amiga users couldnt use the software
anyone wrote in it.

>All in all you sort of feel like you are working on a damn pc when it comes to
>gfx.

I take it that youve never used a GfxCard on your amiga.

>Sorry, but I'll keep working on my AGA-extension.

Have fun, but if its not out soon the new amigas will be out
and it wont work with them.

	Message #2065 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Digest Number 211

(Date unavailable)
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


> It is not possible to display more than one screen at the time.
> As far as I could see, you could not in any way get to some of the nice
> AGA-functions like dual playfield, copper rainbows, dual palettes, etc...

All of these things might have been very nice a few years ago but are
not obsolete. None of these features are available on GFX cards which
is certainly the future (well actually the past for several years
now...)

> Sorry, but I'll keep working on my AGA-extension.

Please do as I hear PAC has given up TGE anyway because of all the
criticism (although this was a few days back).

Just make sure it either support graphics cards or uses mode
promotable screens.

I'm afraid that I feel I'm wasting my time doing anything in AMOS
right now. We badly need a version that will use GFX cards (PPC would
be nice too).

This has of course been a problem for a while but with the release of
Bvision I can't even run an AMOS program without the hassle of
changing my monitor around.


Sorry to be a bit negative. I mean, I've been using AMOS for god
knows how long and have been on this list for several years and have
defended AMOS against a lot of criticism but with the recent moves in
AMIGA's, AMOS has gone from being acceptable if you can program it
well to being unusable.

OH and BTW, Blitz is just as bad, so I'm not advocating that. It's
slightly better with screens but is terrible at other things that AMOS
is good at.

AMOS creators! Any estimates on the future?

-Murray

> AmosPro locks up...

> different fonts

As far as I know it is kind of a bug. Amos Pro doesn't release the memory after
switching fonts (I realized after Amos used up my 128MB of RAM!). I believe
you can use KillLibs (or a command somehting like that) to release the memoty
again.

	Message #2089 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

loading fonts directly

Tue Jan 5, 1999 4:53 am
Cori Skagen <lskagen@ssm.ca>


I found a simple fix my problem about loading fonts directly well sort
of....

just use the Exec command to execute the 'c:setfont fontname size'
and it will load it into memory

then you can use the get rom fonts command

its a hell of alot faster than using the get disc fonts, which can take
forrever if
you have a lot of fonts like I do.

one thing though, I use the comand 'nopaz' instead of setfont (its on
aminet)
because when you execute the setfont command it locks the font into memory
and avail flush won't remove it nopaz doesn't have this problem

if ne1 wants some source for this let me know...
--

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Cori Skagen

lskagen@ssm.ca
ICQ UIN# 22738775
My AMOS page at: www.ssm.ca/lskagen

	Message #2091 of 8234

Re: Not Zero testing

Tue Jan 5, 1999 6:35 am
Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>


Hi Andrew,
> > Just accidentally found a way of testing a variable for >0 or <0
>
> Is it "If A Then...."?
This only says "If A=-1 Then" as checking A in this context is asking
the question "Is A True" (BOOLEEN)
If you say "If Not(A) Then" is the same as saying "If A=0 Then" as
Not(A) is the same as asking "Is A False".

Andy H.

	Message #2093 of 8234

Ship code

Tue Jan 5, 1999 9:50 pm
Sasu Lintula <samali@utu.fi>


This is actually for Leto (sorry, forgot your address), feel free to use...
I added some rems to it:-)
------------------------------------------- 8<
----------------------------------------------------

Screen Open 0,320,256,32,Lowres
Flash Off : Curs Off : Cls

'No double buffer at the moment

Load "python_new.shp" : Get Bob Palette

'Direction Data
Dim SX(32),SY(32)
SX(1)=0 : SX(17)=0 : SY(9)=0 : SY(25)=0
SX(2)=1 : SX(16)=1 : SY(10)=1 : SY(24)=1
SX(3)=2 : SX(15)=2 : SY(11)=2 : SY(23)=2
SX(4)=3 : SX(14)=3 : SY(12)=3 : SY(22)=3
SX(5)=4 : SX(13)=4 : SY(13)=4 : SY(21)=4
SX(6)=5 : SX(12)=5 : SY(14)=5 : SY(20)=5
SX(7)=6 : SX(11)=6 : SY(15)=6 : SY(19)=6
SX(8)=7 : SX(10)=7 : SY(16)=7 : SY(18)=7
SX(9)=8 : SX(25)=-8 : SY(17)=8 : SY(1)=-8
SX(26)=-7 : SX(24)=-7 : SY(31)=-7 : SY(2)=-7
SX(27)=-6 : SX(23)=-6 : SY(30)=-6 : SY(3)=-6
SX(28)=-5 : SX(22)=-6 : SY(29)=-6 : SY(4)=-6
SX(29)=-4 : SX(21)=-4 : SY(28)=-4 : SY(5)=-4
SX(30)=-3 : SX(20)=-3 : SY(27)=-3 : SY(6)=-3
SX(31)=-2 : SX(19)=-2 : SY(26)=-2 : SY(7)=-2
SX(32)=-1 : SX(18)=-1 : SY(25)=-1 : SY(8)=-1

'Ship Controlling
A$="L R0=A ;"
A$=A$+"P: L A=R0 ;"

'Change the following thing if you want to alter ships speed. Last number tells
amal
'how many steps it has to use to move the ship. f.ex. "M RX,RY,1" is bloody fast
'but unplayable. If you use "M RX,RY,16" the ship will glide smoothly but
rotation
'is jerky and too slow. In my opinion "M RX/4,RY/4,4" gives good results.
A$=A$+"M RX/4,RY/4,4 ;"

'Out of Screen?
A$=A$+"I X<0 J C ; I X>320 J F ; I Y<0 J H ; I Y>256 J J ;"

'Joystick
'1=joy up, 2=joy down, 4=joy left, 8=joy right, 16=fire button
A$=A$+"I J1&4 J L ; I J1&8 J R ; K: I J1&16 J T ;"
A$=A$+"L R2=0 ; J P ; "
'
'Turn
A$=A$+"L: L R0=R0-1 ; I R0<1 J I ; J K ; R: L R0=R0+1 ; I R0>32 J D ; J K ;"
A$=A$+"A: L R0=R0-1 ; L RX=RX+RA ; L RY=RY+RB ; I R0<1 J I ; J P;"
A$=A$+"B: L R0=R0+1 ; L RX=RX+RA ; L RY=RY+RB ; I R0>32 J D ; J P;"
A$=A$+"I: L R0=32 ; J K ; D: L R0=1 ; J K ;"
'

'Thurst
A$=A$+"T: L RX=RX+RA ; L RY=RY+RB ; J P ;"
'
'To the Screen
A$=A$+"C: L X=320 ; J P ; F: L X=0 ; J P ; H: L Y=256 ; J P ; J: L Y=0 ; J P ;"

Hide
For N=1 To 32
Hot Spot N,8,8
Next N
Bob 0,160,100,1
Channel 1 To Bob 0
Amal 1,A$
Amal On

Do
S=Amreg(1,0)
If S>32 Then S=1
If S<1 Then S=32
SX=SX(S) : SY=SY(S)
Amreg(0)=SX
Amreg(1)=SY
Loop
------------------------------------------- 8<
----------------------------------------------------

Thats all,

SLin

	Message #2096 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Not Zero testing

Tue Jan 5, 1999 5:21 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>>Just accidentally found a way of testing a variable for >0 or <0
>> Is it "If A Then...."?
>This only says "If A=-1 Then" as checking A in this context is asking
>the question "Is A True" (BOOLEEN)

I used that method for many years, starting on the old C64.
It was a way to squeeze additional speed out of the old interpreted
languages... these days just about everything is compiled so there
is really no need to use it but it still works.


Anything after the "If" is evaluated then tested for non 0.
For example, if you had "If 1+3" 1+3 would be evaluated
creating the temp value of 4.. now the If only checks to see if the
expression failed (EQUALS 0)... 4 is not 0 so the test is true.
However... "If 1+3-4" evaluates to 0 so the test would fail...

Works the same way with variables... in BASIC, C, etc.

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2101 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Not Zero testing

Tue Jan 5, 1999 7:52 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>>> Is it "If A Then...."?
>> This only says "If A=-1 Then" as checking A in this context is asking
>> the question "Is A True" (BOOLEEN)
> Nope, it does If A<>0. Maybe it shouldn't, but it does.

Yep and it should. As long as the expression evaluates to
something other than zero it is true (0 always equals FALSE).

I think the confusion is caused in part by AMOS and some other
languages (generally BASICs) defining True as -1 and not stating
that ANY non zero value is True (in other words as long as it is
not False '0' it must be True). For example, in C programming
TRUE is usually defined as 1 instead of -1.

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

Re: Non amos question

Tue Jan 5, 1999 7:25 am
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 04-Jan-99, Martin Møller wrote:
>From: Martin =?iso-8859-1?Q?M=F8ller?= <tfb@bigfoot.com>

>Hi there, i'm sorry to ask a non amos question here, but i don't know where
>else to ask :(

>My problem is that i'm going on vacation in 2 days.
>And my plan was to bring my old A600 to do my mailing on.

>But the 600 only has 1MB of memory, and none of my internet programs on my
>A1200 seem to work with only 1MB!
>Or maybe it's the 68000 processor? Or both!

>So can someone please tell me if and how i can use a plain A600 to check
>mail on?
>(I need an dialer, and a mail client)

Hmmm...what you'd be best to do would be to get Miami, v3 should work it needs
AOS2.04
which some A600s(if not all) have. Then also get ahold of a telnet client,
like 'AmTelnet' (on aminet). once you have it go online with miami, and then
run telnet, select to connect to your host server, which would normally
be 'text.servername.country' like for me its 'text.iol.ie'. once your on then
you can do anything, and 1mb should be plenty, if not then put wb in 4 colours,
lowres, load miami, go online, then on miami's menu select to iconify, then load
telnet.
telnet works in 2 colours, and only takes up a small window.

Once your connected to your server, you can use their mail software to check
your mails. For me a menu comes up with mail, newsgroups and some other things
on it.
you'll need to have your netpassword handy to get your mails. To use
telnet for getting mails you mostly use the -> and <- cursor keys
rather than return and backspace. it could be diffrent on your server
mine uses 'Pine' so when you log on if it says that then what I have just said
should work.

Yam could also work, but this way will also work off floppies if your
A600 doesnt have a HD. The disadvantage of this is that you have to view your
mails while your online, and you dont save them to your hd, you just read them
from telnet.

>Please, someone help, as the A1200 is to big to bring with me!

voila,

cya,

On 05-Jan-99, Peter Cahill wrote:

I know that this is a tiny trainspotting thing... Sorry.

You often hear "to save memory, set wb in lowres".
This makes no sence - even if the wb is in lowres the width is still minimum
640 pixels. So you won't be saving memory by putting your wb in lowres.
(Well, but the chip-ram-access will be /faster/ in lowres, ofcourse)

EcCalD CopOnOff,0 ; Turn off AMOS-copper
EcCalD CopOnOff,1 ; Turn on AMOS-copper

hw-registers.

	Message #2112 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: TGE - first impression

Wed Jan 6, 1999 10:18 pm
Rune Zedeler <rune@zedeler.dk>


On 06-Jan-99, I wrote:

> EcCalD CopOnOff,0 ; Turn off AMOS-copper
> EcCalD CopOnOff,1 ; Turn on AMOS-copper
>
>When you've turned off the copper you can just "loke" your own values into
>the hw-registers.

Correction.
Use -1 instead of 1 to turn on copper again.
And ofcourse you don't just access the hw-registers that way.
Instead you use

CopWt MACRO ;CopWt x,y
move.w \1,d1
move.w \2,d2
move.w #$1ff,d3
move.w d3,d4
EcCall CopWait
ENDM

CopMv MACRO ;CopMv val.w,HwRegister
move.w \2,d1
move.w \1,d2
EcCall CopMove
ENDM

CopMvL MACRO ;CopMvL val.l,HwRegister
move.w \2,d1
move.l \1,d2
EcCall CopMoveL
ENDM


and you can call

EcCall CopSwap

EcCall CopReset

Personally I'll use those commands as little as possible.
I'll just make a short copper-list wich calls my own copper-list.

Re: TGE - first impression

Wed Jan 6, 1999 10:59 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

>> AMOS does not give the extension programmer any access whatsoever to
its
>> database,
>> to change where to write gfx to or anything like that.

> EcCalD CopOnOff,0 ; Turn off AMOS-copper
> EcCalD CopOnOff,1 ; Turn on AMOS-copper

> When you've turned off the copper you can just "loke" your own values
into the
> hw-registers.

>>> It is not possible to display more than one screen at the time.
>> Thats because of grahpics cards, they dont have a copper.

> That's true. Gfx-cards suxx!!!


GFX card do not suck. You can't say that GFX cards suck, because AGA
*is *an integrated GFX card.

Anyway, AGA may be able to do nice swishy 2d copper stuff, but come
on, what would you rather have:

1. 2D hardware acceleration & copper/blitter with AGA

2. 3D hardware acceleration with Voodoo etc?

See ya.

Well....
Try reading what I was answering to:
"gfx-cards don't have a copper".
If we coun't in AGA as a gfx-card then that statement wouldn't be true.
What i meant was:
Add-on-gfx-cards as they look today suxx.

> Anyway, AGA may be able to do nice swishy 2d copper stuff, but come
>on, what would you rather have:

>1. 2D hardware acceleration & copper/blitter with AGA

>2. 3D hardware acceleration with Voodoo etc?

I agree that AGA is far too slow. But...
I just think that all those 3D things are fancy add-ons - and with the basics
(vbl-timing, copper, timing after audio-device, etc) not working satisfacting
I find it quite rediculous with a lot of add-ons.
I concider all those gfx-cards somewhat like pyramids build upsite-down; - the
top is huge - but it doesn't have a fundament.

I think the basics are the most important things. - Not fancy gfx.

	Message #2148 of 8234

Re: Grabbing

Sun Jan 10, 1999 1:20 pm
Ken <cbminfo@digital.net>


>> I was wondering if anyone knew if it was possible to grab a screen
>> from within amos, e.g. the workbench screen???
>> any help would be greatly appreciated!

I have no idea what this thing does, as I haven't figured out how to do 1/10
the things in amos yet. But while looking for tutors to amos I did run across
this on aminet.

Short: Grab AMOS screens (developers only)
Author: keller@vip.cybercity.dk
Uploader: keller@vip.cybercity.dk
Type: dev/amos


AMOSGrab 1.00 - Read Me
-----------------------
1. What is AMOSGrab
-------------------
AMOSGrab is a short chunk of code that allows AMOS developers to do some
decent screengrabs. Only a few ordinary screengrabbers does AMOS screens and
none of them is able to grab sprite nor bobs - AMOSGrab can!

Is this what you have in mind ? I suspect it's something you have to add to
your own program.

Re: Grabbing

Sun Jan 10, 1999 3:03 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 10-Jan-99, Ken wrote:

> I have no idea what this thing does, as I haven't figured out how to do 1/10
> the things in amos yet. But while looking for tutors to amos I did run
across
> this on aminet.

> Short: Grab AMOS screens (developers only)

> AMOSGrab is a short chunk of code that allows AMOS developers to do some
> decent screengrabs. Only a few ordinary screengrabbers does AMOS screens and
> none of them is able to grab sprite nor bobs - AMOSGrab can!

> Is this what you have in mind ? I suspect it's something you have to add to
> your own program.

Well I know what it does - I made it :) AMOSGrab is a grabber for AMOS
screens.
As you might know AMOS doesn't use standard screens and thus you can't grab it
with a standard grabber. This grabber allows AMOS coders to eg. grab a screen
from their game. Boy, I gotta start making some better docs...

	Message #2152 of 8234 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Sprite / Bob grabber

Sun Jan 10, 1999 4:02 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>I realised the other day that I do not have a bob/sprite grabber.
>Can anyone tell me which ones are (is) the best and where/how to get it.

I don't know about the best but I threw one together last year to aid in
the development of my CBATNAM stage... certainly is less tedious
than the Bob/Sprite Grabber which came with AMOS. :)

I think it is still on my website... called AutoImageGrabber.
Gets its name from the fact that it automatically scans an IFF Screen,
grabs all of the images and stores them in either the Bob or Icon bank
depending on which you have chosen to work with. It is very fast too!!
Anyway, check http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam
From there go to the Amiga page then AMOS page...

Hmm... now if only I could find the source for that version... LOL

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #2167 of 8234

Easy AMOS

Tue Jan 12, 1999 10:12 am
Tony Gray <tony_gray@uk.ibm.com>


Hi Andrew,

Easy AMOS isn't the best version of AMOS unless you really are a REAL beginner
in programming
and I doubt that it would be capable of producing a football game.

I'm presuming you mean a Sensi-Soccer type game rather Premier Manager. A
sensi-soccer game
is going to be tricky as AMOS, although very versatile, is not particularly
quick.

If you have some programming skills, and want to program in AMOS, then get a
copy of AMOS Pro
and the AMOS Pro compiler. Get to know the language by coding smaller projects
and then build slowly
to the type of game you want to produce.

Cheers

Tony

	Message #2173 of 8234

Re: Grabbing

Tue Jan 12, 1999 2:03 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


-----Original Message-----
From: Lee Marchment <Lee@rgb-bbs.freeserve.co.uk>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 09 January 1999 18:42
Subject: [amos-list] Grabbing


>From: Lee Marchment <Lee@rgb-bbs.freeserve.co.uk>
>
>Hi,
>I was wondering if anyone knew if it was possible to grab a screen from
>within amos, e.g. the workbench screen???
>any help would be greatly appreciated!
>if not do you any screen grabbers which use AREXX?
>thanks!

Yes you can do it by getting hold of the workbech rastport or screen
handle... and then reading the bit planes directly in. I have a piece of
code to do this which is a bit unstable as it hasn't really been bug checked
but I'll get back to you! ( My famous last Words! )

Well hang on... I'll just get part of the code... The bit that grabs the
workbench handle. No hang on... I'll sort out the bugs now.....
BRB!!

+-----------------------+
¦   Start of Program    ¦
+-----------------------+

' Program By Phil Glanville And Andi Allen!
' +--------------------------------------+
' | This Program is Design to Grab The   |
' | WorkBench Screen and Copy it to a    |
' | Public Screen. Or Depending on the   |
' | Amount of Colours Your Workbench     |
' | Uses to an Amos Screen! Have Fun!    |
' | You will notice a slight difference  |
' | In the Quality of Colour.. Because   |
' | Workbench Uses a RRGGBB Screen and   |
' | Amos Only uses RGB Screens!          |
' +-------------------------------------+
' *-------- SNAKEByte SOFTWare ---------*

' Stop This Program Ending to soon!

Break On

' Grab The Workbench Handle / RastPort!

GRABWBHAND
WHAN=Param

' Find the Workbench Parameters..
' Although I haven't got a bit that Finds Hires
' or Lowres.

DPTH=Peek(WHAN+189)
CLRS=Deek(Leek(WHAN+48)+2)
WDTH=Deek(WHAN+12)
HGHT=Deek(WHAN+14)
BPRW=WDTH/8

If CLRS<=64

Amos To Front

' An Ordinary Amos Screen Can handle these Colours so..

If CLRS>16
Screen Open 0,WDTH,HGHT,CLRS,Lowres
Else
Screen Open 0,WDTH,HGHT,CLRS,Hires
End If

Flash Off
Curs Off
Blit Clear -1

' The Palette Locations on the Source Screen.
SCLR=Leek(Leek(WHAN+48)+4)

' The Bit That Copies The Source Palette to the Dest.

For I=0 To CLRS-1
I2=I*2
CL$=Hex$(Deek(SCLR+I2))-"$"
CL$=Space$(3-Len(CL$))+CL$
R=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,1,1))
G=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,2,1))
B=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,3,1))
Colour I,Jd Rgb Value(R,G,B)
Next I

' The Part That Copies The Bitplanes of the Source Screen
' To that of the Destination. But for some strange reason
' Its not as simple as it sounds! The Bitplanes of the
' Workbench screen Are offset by one to the Public Screen
' And Also Each line of Image data seems to be seperated
' buy other lines of stuff. So it is'nt just a simple
' Copy Each bitplane you have to copy each line!

U=0
LWHAN=WHAN+192

For I=0 To DPTH-1
Add U,1,0 To DPTH-1
WLB=Leek(LWHAN+U*4)-BPRW
If U=0
P=DPTH
Else
P=0
End If
SLB=Logbase(I)
For O=0 To HGHT-1
Copy WLB+P*BPRW,WLB+P*BPRW+BPRW To SLB+O*BPRW
Add P,DPTH
Next O
Next I

Break Off
Wait Key

Else

Amos To Back

' The Colours of the Workbench are more than an Amos Screen
' Without AGA Compatiblity Can Handle. So Lets Use A Public
' Screen as an Output!

' Open The Public Screen And get The Handle!

OPENSCREEN[0,0,WDTH,HGHT,DPTH,1,3,Hires,$10F,0,0,0,"PUB_Screen"]
SHAN=Param

' The Palette Locations on the Source and destination Screen.
SCLR=Leek(Leek(WHAN+48)+4)
DCLR=Leek(Leek(SHAN+48)+4)

' The Bit That Copies The Source Palette to the Dest.

For I=0 To CLRS-1
I2=I*2
CL$=Hex$(Deek(SCLR+I2))-"$"
CL$=Space$(3-Len(CL$))+CL$
R=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,1,1))
G=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,2,1))
B=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,3,1))
Doke DCLR+I2,Jd Rgb Value(R,G,B)
Next I

' The Part That Copies The Bitplanes of the Source Screen
' To that of the Destination. But for some strange reason
' Its not as simple as it sounds! The Bitplanes of the
' Workbench screen Are offset by one to the Public Screen
' And Also Each line of Image data seems to be seperated
' buy other lines of stuff. So it is'nt just a simple
' Copy Each bitplane you have to copy each line!

U=0
LWHAN=WHAN+192
LSHAN=SHAN+192

For I=0 To DPTH-1
Add U,1,0 To DPTH-1
WLB=Leek(LWHAN+U*4)-BPRW
If U=0
P=DPTH
Else
P=0
End If
SLB=Leek(LSHAN+(I*4))
For O=0 To HGHT-1
Copy WLB+P*BPRW,WLB+P*BPRW+BPRW To SLB+O*BPRW
Add P,DPTH
Next O
Next I

' The Screen update to refresh the colours!

NULL=Intcall(-384)

' Wait for Escape!

Repeat
Until Key State(69)=-1

' Close The Public Screen!

VEOP:
Amos To Front
Areg(0)=SHAN
VOID=Intcall(-66)
Break Off

End If

End

' The Procedures!
Procedure GRABWBHAND
S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
S=Intcall(-510)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
Areg(1)=0
NULL=Intcall(-516)
End Proc[S]
Procedure OPENSCREEN[X,Y,W,H,D,F,B,V,S,C,G,M,T$]
T$=T$+Chr$(0)
T=Varptr(T$)
Reserve As Work 99,32
A=Start(99)
Doke A,X
Add A,2
Doke A,Y
Add A,2
Doke A,W
Add A,2
Doke A,H
Add A,2
Doke A,D
Add A,2
Poke A,F
Add A,1
Poke A,B
Add A,1
Doke A,V
Add A,2
Doke A,S
Add A,2
Loke A,C
Add A,4
Loke A,T
Add A,4
Loke A,G
Add A,4
Loke A,M
Areg(0)=Start(99)
H=Intcall(-198)
Erase 99
End Proc[H]

+----------------------+
¦    End of Program    ¦
+----------------------+

Thar U go! I have tested it now and so far no bugs... So tell me if you find
anything!
Oh and if anyone can sort it out so that the Public screen I open can Be
RRGGBB
then i would be very gratefull. Although i have not tried it this should
work for any
screen as long as you get the right handle but this has been specifically
made
for Workbench and Workbench has a very strange screen system compared to
Public Screens so It most probably would work... And knowing my luck it most
probably wont so i'm working on it!

Phil! ... SNAKEByte SOFTWare!

	Message #2197 of 8234

Re: Ordering Polygons!

Wed Jan 13, 1999 3:08 am
Andy H <geosync@space.net.au>


Hi John,

The best way to order polygons is to set up a Z-Buffer. It`s a memory
bank that stores the depth (along the Z axis) of each pixel as it is
drawn to the screen. When another pixel tries to write to the same
pixel it checks the Z-buffer. If the current pixel is closer then it
gets drawn on the screen and is added to the Z-buffer.

Andy H.

> Hey! There.... Just a quick message does anyone out there know a good way of
> ordering polygons... What i mean is when drawing a 3d object... the polgons
> need to be draw in an order so that the things in the background are in the
> background!

	Message #2205 of 8249

FW: GFX Adventure

Wed Jan 13, 1999 3:36 pm
"Ives, Neil, IVESNJ" <neil.ives@bt.com>


> Can anyone help me modify a procedure which provides the inventory of a
> graphic adventure (Monkey Island style).

> It currently displays the inventory in text on-screen, but I would like it
> to show small thumbnails of the object instead.

I think if I was doing this I would be using an array to store the status of
items collected. For instance the key to the cellar could be allocated item
number 1 and when picked up its flag could be changed to true etc.
When required the array could be read and small icons corresponding to the
used inventory item number could be pasted to screen. In the same way the
item status can be changed to false when it has been used or put down etc.
The items and arrays could be set up at the beginning and used at any time
during the game.

I would be interested to hear of better methods from the experts on the
list.

	Message #2210 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: runnable program

Wed Jan 13, 1999 6:24 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>Using this coverdisk amos, moving along with the learning amos procedure, I
>found I have no way to save a runnable program. Only way to run anything
>(that I can see) is to also include a copy of this coverdisk AMOSPRO with
>every program made. Am I missing something here ?

Hahahaha... well, that AMOS development system you are using (actually
any of them that anyone uses) to WRITE your programs is an interpreter.
You are writing the source code for the program... which is tokenized but
not compiled. This source code has no meaning to anything outside of
the AMOS Interpreter.

To create a "runnable program" as you call it (also known as an
executable) you need a tool known as a compiler. The Amos Compiler
will compile the AMOS Source code you have written into a binary
executable file which may be "run" completely independant of the
AMOS Interpreter Environment.

There was another method known as the RAMOS RunTim Distribution
System but that was akind of quirky and besides the Compiler should
easily double your program's speed.

I can send you the AMOSv1.36 compiler in source code form... just load it
as an accessory and compile. Hmm, you are using AMOSPro though so
that compiler might not work... well, I do have the AMOSPro Compiler as
well. :-)

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2215 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

MPD FTP Site now taking uploads

Wed Jan 13, 1999 11:35 pm
"Andy \"Mushroom\" Kellett" <mushypd@redrose.net>


Ive turned the upload feature back on the FTP site. Many thanks to all
those who have already been on the site looking around, and most probably
noticed that it hasnt changed very much in the last couple of months.

I know there are lots of you out there who have a project/game/source thats
finished and would like the public to be able to gain access to it. Well
now you can! Use your ftp client to log in anonymously to my FTP site, and
go into /pub/amiga/amos/uploads and store it there, along with a .Readme
file explaining where abouts in the FTP site you think it belongs, and a
description of what is contained in the archives. All files without readme
files will be erased. The readme should be kept in the same manner as below:



Short: A one-line description of your archive
Type: source/game or any folder you wish to use
Author: Your name <email address>
Uploader: Uploader Name <uploader Email address>

Then follows a large description of your program. This can be as big as you
want, but try and keep it under 10K in size if possible.


Once in the folder, i will look at it and then transfer it over to the main
folder where anyone can download and look at it. If you have any questions,
feel free to email me.

Andy Kellett
mushypd@redrose.net

>Hi John,
>
>The best way to order polygons is to set up a Z-Buffer. It`s a memory
>bank that stores the depth (along the Z axis) of each pixel as it is
>drawn to the screen. When another pixel tries to write to the same
>pixel it checks the Z-buffer. If the current pixel is closer then it
>gets drawn on the screen and is added to the Z-buffer.

of each of the polgons i have to draw?

I'm not sure if it would work! Could you explain further?

	Message #2226 of 8249

Re: Ordering Polygons!

Thu Jan 14, 1999 11:46 pm
Andy H <geosync@space.net.au>


Hi John,

Yes it would be slow on a 68020/30 unless you wrote it in machine code.
Also you can poke the data straight in the memory bank to get a speed
increase. Really the best way to go about this is either develop it on
a 68060 or get someone on this list to write a machine-code plugin for
AMOS that sets up the ZBuffer for you. The other way is to write it in
C/C++.
Instead you could implement a simplified sorting routine that keeps
track of the relative distance from the screen, each polygon takes up.
This will not allow polygons to interweave as the ZBuffer will allow but
it will give you all the polygons at the right depth.
1. Get the relative distance by finding the average Z range of all the
points in the first polygon / or just take one of the current polygon's
z coords.
2. Store a pointer to the polygon (don`t draw it yet) in a table /
array. Have two arrays one called 'Work(X)' and 'Buffer(X)'.
3. Get the next polygon and compare it to the ones in the list. At
this stage you go thru 'Work(X)' comparing the current poly with each
poly stored. If the stored poly is closer, put that one in the
'Buffer(x)' and move to the next poly in 'Work(X)', otherwise copy the
current poly to 'Buffer(X)' and then copy all remaining poly's from
'Work(x)' into 'Buffer(x)' under the last poly. At the end of each
sort, copy the entire 'Buffer(x)' to 'Work(x)'.
4. In the end 'Work(x)' will contain a list of depth sorted polys. You
start at the bottom and work to the top of the array, drawing the
polygons found in the array. Depending on your viewport depth you start
drawing polys further up the array, always working backward to the first
(closest) poly. This is the painters algorithm.

Hope this helps, email again if you have more questions.
Andy H.
> >
> >The best way to order polygons is to set up a Z-Buffer. It`s a memory
> >bank that stores the depth (along the Z axis) of each pixel as it is
> >drawn to the screen. When another pixel tries to write to the same
> >pixel it checks the Z-buffer. If the current pixel is closer then it
> >gets drawn on the screen and is added to the Z-buffer.
>
> Okay would that just be a slight bit slow having to read in all the pixels
> of each of the polgons i have to draw?
>
> I'm not sure if it would work! Could you explain further?
>

Re: Where's AMOS?

Fri Jan 15, 1999 2:51 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>Hi everybody!
>As much as I'd like to get my hands on that elusive AMOS Professional,
>it seems that nowhere sells it! It's not in any shops, any second hand
>goods shops, and I've placed adverts in the newspaper. Is it anywhere?
>To combat this problem, I've bought another games engine - Gamesmith.
>I haven't got it yet but I hope it will be okay...

Gamesmith is a library... it is intended primarily for C/Assembler
programmers who want an easier method to handle the audio/video
aspects of Amiga programming.

I have the Gamesmith library but was not that impressed with its speed.
It is roughly 2-3x faster than AMOS but not quite as fast as it could be.
I did not care much for the way you set up screens either as it is almost
exactly the same method as you use in pure OS-style coding. I was
expecting a more straight-forward parameter oriented style using simple
values rather than pointers and structures. Of course, we could simply
write some wrappers around the more cumbersome "commands" so it
is not that big of a problem.
They deserve some credit as Gamesmith does a LOT to make Amiga
C/Assembler programming an easier task and also Gamesmith is much
more stable than GMS.
Actually, we could just make a few wrappers around the more cumbersome
Gamesmith screen "commands" and kind of AMOSfy the whole thing.
Also, you should be receiving the second release version which might
address the screen issue and be faster too.

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2232 of 8249

Re: Ordering Polygons!

Fri Jan 15, 1999 11:42 am
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


-----Original Message-----
From: Andy H <geosync@space.net.au>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 14 January 1999 23:45
Subject: [amos-list] Re: Ordering Polygons!


>From: Andy H <geosync@space.net.au>
>
>Hi John,
>
>Yes it would be slow on a 68020/30 unless you wrote it in machine code.
>Also you can poke the data straight in the memory bank to get a speed
>increase. Really the best way to go about this is either develop it on
>a 68060 or get someone on this list to write a machine-code plugin for
>AMOS that sets up the ZBuffer for you. The other way is to write it in
>C/C++.
>Instead you could implement a simplified sorting routine that keeps
>track of the relative distance from the screen, each polygon takes up.
>This will not allow polygons to interweave as the ZBuffer will allow but
>it will give you all the polygons at the right depth.
>1. Get the relative distance by finding the average Z range of all the
>points in the first polygon / or just take one of the current polygon's
>z coords.
>2. Store a pointer to the polygon (don`t draw it yet) in a table /
>array. Have two arrays one called 'Work(X)' and 'Buffer(X)'.
>3. Get the next polygon and compare it to the ones in the list. At
>this stage you go thru 'Work(X)' comparing the current poly with each
>poly stored. If the stored poly is closer, put that one in the
>'Buffer(x)' and move to the next poly in 'Work(X)', otherwise copy the
>current poly to 'Buffer(X)' and then copy all remaining poly's from
>'Work(x)' into 'Buffer(x)' under the last poly. At the end of each
>sort, copy the entire 'Buffer(x)' to 'Work(x)'.
>4. In the end 'Work(x)' will contain a list of depth sorted polys. You
>start at the bottom and work to the top of the array, drawing the
>polygons found in the array. Depending on your viewport depth you start
>drawing polys further up the array, always working backward to the first
>(closest) poly. This is the painters algorithm.
>

Thanx... It sounds like i need to rewite my 3D system... as at the moment it
is optimised just for wireframe rendering.... I'll get back to you... Thanx
Again!

C-Ya.,...

PHIL!.................SNAKEByte SOFTWare!

>Andy H.

	Message #2236 of 8249

Re: Thanks 4 the grabber

Fri Jan 15, 1999 2:23 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Okay I have very little knolege of networking and things... i've tried
reading from the parralel port and stuff like that but to no avail! I do
know about screens tho... and as long as the VidiAmiga12 screen is
classified as a screen you can grab it..... I'll send you some code!

hang on! =o)

Okay this program Basically tells you a lot about each of the screens that
are
open at the time it is run.... Run it and scan throught the information
until you get
to the VIDIAMIGA12 Screen.... It should have a name! if not I can't really
help
because at the moment i'm still trying to find a way of identifying screens
that don't
have names... But if it does have a name... Email it to me and i'll write
you a piece of
code that grabs that specific screen for you!

* START OF CODE *
----------------------------
Screen Open 0,640,256,4,Hires
Flash Off
Curs Off
Paper 0
Ink 2
Pen 2
Cls 0

Break Off
Amos Lock
Amos To Front

OPENSCREEN[0,0,320,256,6,1,3,Lowres,$10F,0,0,0,"LISTScreens"]
SHAN=Param
NHAN=SHAN

Gr Writing 0

Repeat

' Top Coordinates of the screen
XTOP=Deek(NHAN+8)
YTOP=Deek(NHAN+10)
' Dimentions width and Height of screen
WDTH=Deek(NHAN+12)
HGHT=Deek(NHAN+14)
' Mouse coordinates on screen
XMCO=Deek(NHAN+16)
YMCO=Deek(NHAN+18)
' Bytes per row, How many bytes are used for each line
' Of the screen!
BPRW=Deek(NHAN+184)
' How many rows / Lines of the screen
ROWS=Deek(NHAN+186)
' Flags... I'm not sure what they are for!
BFLG=Peek(NHAN+188)
' The depth of the screen... How many Bitplanes.
DPTH=Peek(NHAN+189)
' Not sure what this is but its called PAD.
PADS=Deek(NHAN+190)
' The Colour Map... The Location of the ColourMap
CMAP=Leek(NHAN+48)
' The Colour Flags
CFLG=Peek(CMAP+0)
' The Type? Don't know
TYPE=Peek(CMAP+1)
' The amount of colours on the screen
CLRS=Deek(CMAP+2)
' The Address of the colour Table... Palette!
CTAB=Leek(CMAP+4)

' The name of the Screen
NAME$=Peek$(Leek(NHAN+22),80,Chr$(0))
If NAME$=""
NAME$="Unnamed Screen."
End If

Print "SCREEN : ";NAME$
Print "X TOP :";XTOP
Print "Y TOP :";YTOP
Print "WIDTH :";WDTH
Print "HEIGHT :";HGHT
Print "XMOUSE :";XMCO
Print "YMOUSE :";YMCO
Print
Print "C MAP :"
Print "FLAGS :";CFLG
Print "TYPE :";TYPE
Print "COLORS :";CLRS
Print "C TABLE: ";Hex$(CTAB)
Print
Print "BITMAP :"
Print "DEPTH :";DPTH
Print "FLAGS :";BFLG
Print "PAD :";PADS
Print "ROWS :";ROWS
Print "BIT/ROW:";BPRW

' Out put the Logbases / Bitplanes of the screen dependant
' on the depth
For U=0 To DPTH-1
Print "LOGB";U;" :";Leek(NHAN+192+U*4)
Next U

' Print out the palette of the screen
' Making sure it fits on the screen
X=0
K=0
Z=1
Repeat
Locate 30+X,Z
Print Hex$(Deek(CTAB+K*2))
Inc K
If Z=29
X=X+5
End If
Add Z,1,1 To 29
Until K=CLRS

Locate 60,30
Print "< Press a Key >"
Wait Key
Cls 0
Locate 0,0

' The next screen's base
NHAN=Leek(NHAN)

Until NHAN=0 or Key State(69)

KLOSESCREEN[SHAN]
Break On
Amos Unlock
Amos To Front
End

Procedure OPENSCREEN[X,Y,W,H,D,F,B,V,S,C,G,M,T$]

T$=T$+Chr$(0)
T=Varptr(T$)
Reserve As Work 99,32
A=Start(99)

Doke A,X : Add A,2 : Rem x pos
Doke A,Y : Add A,2 : Rem y pos
Doke A,W : Add A,2 : Rem width
Doke A,H : Add A,2 : Rem height
Doke A,D : Add A,2 : Rem depth
Poke A,F : Add A,1 : Rem detail pen
Poke A,B : Add A,1 : Rem block pen
Doke A,V : Add A,2 : Rem view modes
Doke A,S : Add A,2 : Rem screen type
Loke A,C : Add A,4 : Rem font
Loke A,T : Add A,4 : Rem title
Loke A,G : Add A,4 : Rem gadgets
Loke A,M : Rem address of bitmap

Areg(0)=Start(99)
H=Intcall(-198)
Erase 99

End Proc[H]
Procedure KLOSESCREEN[H]

Areg(0)=H : Rem screen handle
VOID=Intcall(-66)

End Proc
-------------------------
* End of Program *

And here is the code for the WBGrabber without the JD ext.

*Start of Code*
-------------------

' Program By Phil Glanville And Andi Allen!
' +--------------------------------------+
' | This Program is Design to Grab The   |
' | WorkBench Screen and Copy it to a    |
' | Public Screen. Or Depending on the   |
' | Amount of Colours Your Workbench     |
' | Uses to an Amos Screen! Have Fun!    |
' | You will notice a slight difference  |
' | In the Quality of Colour.. Because   |
' | Workbench Uses a RRGGBB Screen and   |
' | Amos Only uses RGB Screens!          |
' +-------------------------------------+
' *-------- SNAKEByte SOFTWare ---------*

' Stop This Program Ending to soon!

Break On

' Grab The Workbench Handle / RastPort!

GRABWBHAND
WHAN=Param

' Find the Workbench Parameters..
' Although I haven't got a bit that Finds Hires
' or Lowres.

DPTH=Peek(WHAN+189)
CLRS=Deek(Leek(WHAN+48)+2)
WDTH=Deek(WHAN+12)
HGHT=Deek(WHAN+14)
BPRW=WDTH/8

If CLRS<=64

Amos To Front

' An Ordinary Amos Screen Can handle these Colours so..

If CLRS>16
Screen Open 0,WDTH,HGHT,CLRS,Lowres
Else
Screen Open 0,WDTH,HGHT,CLRS,Hires
End If

Flash Off
Curs Off
Blit Clear -1

' The Palette Locations on the Source Screen.
SCLR=Leek(Leek(WHAN+48)+4)

' The Bit That Copies The Source Palette to the Dest.

For I=0 To CLRS-1
I2=I*2
CL$=Hex$(Deek(SCLR+I2))-"$"
CL$=Space$(3-Len(CL$))+CL$
R=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,1,1))
G=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,2,1))
B=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,3,1))
Colour I,R*256+G*16+B
Next I

' The Part That Copies The Bitplanes of the Source Screen
' To that of the Destination. But for some strange reason
' Its not as simple as it sounds! The Bitplanes of the
' Workbench screen Are offset by one to the Public Screen
' And Also Each line of Image data seems to be seperated
' buy other lines of stuff. So it is'nt just a simple
' Copy Each bitplane you have to copy each line!

U=0
LWHAN=WHAN+192

For I=0 To DPTH-1
Add U,1,0 To DPTH-1
WLB=Leek(LWHAN+U*4)-BPRW
If U=0
P=DPTH
Else
P=0
End If
SLB=Logbase(I)
For O=0 To HGHT-1
Copy WLB+P*BPRW,WLB+P*BPRW+BPRW To SLB+O*BPRW
Add P,DPTH
Next O
Next I

Break Off
Wait Key

Else

Amos To Back

' The Colours of the Workbench are more than an Amos Screen
' Without AGA Compatiblity Can Handle. So Lets Use A Public
' Screen as an Output!

' Open The Public Screen And get The Handle!

OPENSCREEN[0,0,WDTH,HGHT,DPTH,1,3,Hires,$10F,0,0,0,"PUB_Screen"]
SHAN=Param

' The Palette Locations on the Source and destination Screen.
SCLR=Leek(Leek(WHAN+48)+4)
DCLR=Leek(Leek(SHAN+48)+4)

' The Bit That Copies The Source Palette to the Dest.

For I=0 To CLRS-1
I2=I*2
CL$=Hex$(Deek(SCLR+I2))-"$"
CL$=Space$(3-Len(CL$))+CL$
R=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,1,1))
G=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,2,1))
B=Val("$"+Mid$(CL$,3,1))
Doke DCLR+I2,R*256+G*16+B
Next I

' The Part That Copies The Bitplanes of the Source Screen
' To that of the Destination. But for some strange reason
' Its not as simple as it sounds! The Bitplanes of the
' Workbench screen Are offset by one to the Public Screen
' And Also Each line of Image data seems to be seperated
' buy other lines of stuff. So it is'nt just a simple
' Copy Each bitplane you have to copy each line!

U=0
LWHAN=WHAN+192
LSHAN=SHAN+192

For I=0 To DPTH-1
Add U,1,0 To DPTH-1
WLB=Leek(LWHAN+U*4)-BPRW
If U=0
P=DPTH
Else
P=0
End If
SLB=Leek(LSHAN+(I*4))
For O=0 To HGHT-1
Copy WLB+P*BPRW,WLB+P*BPRW+BPRW To SLB+O*BPRW
Add P,DPTH
Next O
Next I

' The Screen update to refresh the colours!

NULL=Intcall(-384)

' Wait for Escape!

Repeat
Until Key State(69)=-1

' Close The Public Screen!

VEOP:
Amos To Front
Areg(0)=SHAN
VOID=Intcall(-66)
Break Off

End If

End

' The Procedures!
Procedure GRABWBHAND
S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
S=Intcall(-510)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
Areg(1)=0
NULL=Intcall(-516)
End Proc[S]
Procedure OPENSCREEN[X,Y,W,H,D,F,B,V,S,C,G,M,T$]
T$=T$+Chr$(0)
T=Varptr(T$)
Reserve As Work 99,32
A=Start(99)
Doke A,X
Add A,2
Doke A,Y
Add A,2
Doke A,W
Add A,2
Doke A,H
Add A,2
Doke A,D
Add A,2
Poke A,F
Add A,1
Poke A,B
Add A,1
Doke A,V
Add A,2
Doke A,S
Add A,2
Loke A,C
Add A,4
Loke A,T
Add A,4
Loke A,G
Add A,4
Loke A,M
Areg(0)=Start(99)
H=Intcall(-198)
Erase 99
End Proc[H]


-------------------
*End of code*

I hope the code helps!

Phil!................ SNAKEByte SOFTWare!

Re: Finding attributes

Fri Jan 15, 1999 9:45 pm
"Keith Hill" <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


>Can anyone tell me how I can find what the pen & paper colours are at
>a given print position or the ink colours are at a pixel coordinate?
>
>For example, if I have Locate 10,10 , how can I find what the existing
colours
>are?


Ummm... you can't as such, but you can find out the pixel colours at a
coord. Try something like
test=point (x*8,y*8)
Yeah, I know its messy, but you could scan all the pixels in the 8*8 grid.

Re: Finding attributes

Fri Jan 15, 1999 9:48 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> From: Alan Stevens <alans@...>

> Can anyone tell me how I can find what the pen & paper colours are at
> a given print position or the ink colours are at a pixel coordinate?

> For example, if I have Locate 10,10 , how can I find what the existing
colours
> are?

Well, you can't get the pen/paper colour, but you can get the pixle
colour at x,y with P=point(x,y)

(eg, for your locate example: P=Point(80,80) would give the paper
colour anyway).

Re: ASCII Reader

Sat Jan 16, 1999 10:08 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>

Hi Everybody,

> From: r!K <rik@riks-room.freeserve.co.uk>

> Hi,
> I'm having a few probs atm, hopefully you guys can be some help.
> What I want to do is read an ascii text file and display it on the
screen.
> read the file like so:

> #f$=fsel$("blahblah"..)#
> #If Exist(f$)#
> # Open In 1,f$ : SIZE=Lof(1)#
> # Reserve As Data 1,SIZE#
> # Bload 1,f$#
> #end if#

> But I can't figure out how to display the thing on the screen.
> I suspect it may be Loke,Doke,Peek,Poke etc but I have no clue how to
use
> them.......

Just ascii text? you don't want to do it like that, do it like this:


max_lines=1000
dim lines$(max_lines)
#f$=fsel$("blahblah"..)#
line_no=0
#If Exist(f$)#
open in 1,f$
repeat
input #1,lines$(line_no)
line_no=line_no+1
until eof(1)
end if


that'll load that text file into the string array. now you can just
print the lines off.
(line_no will hold how many lines there are)

See ya.

the basics

Sat Jan 16, 1999 8:44 pm
Ken <cbminfo@digital.net>


Running thru some of the demos I found, I ran across this interesting one and
tried to dissect it to see exactly what it was doing..

Here's the actual code with comments removed. This doesn't work.
it hits the 1st unpack and tells me 'bank not reserved at line 2'

Hide On
Unpack 10 To 0 : Screen Hide
Unpack 9 To 1 : Screen Hide

the unpack 10 to 0.
Here's the actual program with comments to the above lines.

' *************************************
' *                                   *
' *      Dual Playfield Demo V1.0     *
' *      Written by Chris Hodges      *
' *                                   *
' *************************************
'
' Weg mit der Maus!
Hide On
' Zuerst entpacken wir den Hintergrund. Größe: 640x200x8.
' Der Bereich von (320,0)-(640,200) ist noch leer.
Unpack 10 To 0 : Screen Hide
' Dann den Vordergrund. Größe: 640x200x8.
Unpack 9 To 1 : Screen Hide
' Jetzt kopieren wir den Background, damit er cyclic wird.

I went and saved the entire file as ascii, then just imported as ascii. Then
tried running. Comments have zip to do with it. Something during the loading
seems to be doing the reserving and setting up the screen background, a blue
and white marbled effect.

anyone say whats missing here ?

	Message #2258 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: the basics

Sun Jan 17, 1999 12:10 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> Running thru some of the demos I found, I ran across this interesting
one and
> tried to dissect it to see exactly what it was doing..

> Here's the actual code with comments removed. This doesn't work.
> it hits the 1st unpack and tells me 'bank not reserved at line 2'

> Hide On
> Unpack 10 To 0 : Screen Hide
> Unpack 9 To 1 : Screen Hide

> the unpack 10 to 0.
> Here's the actual program with comments to the above lines.

OK, the problems simple. The graphics are saved with the source in
the .AMOS file. Once you convert it to ascii that data is lost, so the
program doesn't work.

The way to get around it is to load it into amos, go to direct and
type

Save "work:AMOS/9.abk",9
Save "work:AMOS/10.abk",10

(change path etc.)


then at the start of the program add

Load "work:AMOS/9.abk",9
Load "work:AMOS/10.abk",10



That should do it...

See ya.

>#f$=fsel$("blahblah"..)#
>#If Exist(f$)#
># Open In 1,f$ : SIZE=Lof(1)#
># Reserve As Data 1,SIZE#
># Bload 1,f$#
>#end if#
>
>But I can't figure out how to display the thing on the screen.
>I suspect it may be Loke,Doke,Peek,Poke etc but I have no clue how to use
>them.......
>
>Also, I don,t really want to have to use COMMAND$="blah" and call an
>amigados command to view the text.
>
>Any help, tips, source, examples etc would be most appreciated =)
>

Okay heres a thing of the top of my head....
Well not the first bit!!! =O)

What this hopefully does is print the text to the screen.... but it ignores
all formatting
so if you want to view it like a text file as like you are seeing this email
now... Its not
what you want... its what i use to view files that have binary in them as
most of my text editors and things can't load it properly... I hope this
help although its most probably not what your looking for!
If you want it formatted use the other guys source!

Screen Open 0,640,256,16,32768
Colour 1,$0
Flash Off
Curs Off
Cls 0
Ink 5
' Load in the file!
F$=Fsel$("")
Open In 1,F$
LFO=Lof(1)
Close 1
Reserve As Work 8,LFO
Bload F$,8
ST8=Start(8)
NR8=(LFO/80)*80
KEY=1
Do
Repeat
If Key State(77)=-1
POS=POS+80
' This bit checks to see if the end of the
' text file is at the bottom of the screen
If POS+2400>NR8
POS=NR8-2400
End If
KEY=1
End If
If Key State(76)=-1
POS=POS-80
' This bit checks to see if we have
' reached the topof the file!
If POS<0
POS=0
End If
KEY=1
End If
Until KEY=1

' Checks to see if the file is smaller than the
' screen if so the screen cannot move up or down!
If LFO<2400
POS=0
End If
KEY=0
KU=80
' Now the printing bit!
For I=0 To 30
If POS+(I*80)+KU>LFO
KU=LFO-(POS+(I*80))
End If
If KU<0
Exit
End If
Text 0,6+I*8,Peek$(ST8+POS+(I*80),KU)+Space$(80-KU)
Next I

Loop

Hope it helps!
Phil.............................SNAKEByte SOFTWare!

I think andrew was just trying to give you an idea of what to do...
The code he supplied just stores the lines of text in an array - it
doesn't print it. You's need something like:
For x=0 to line_no
Print line$(x)
If x=30 :Rem or however many lines AMOS can show down the screen
Wait Key
Cls
Endif
Next

...oh yes, and I'm presuming you're not tying those hashes on the 3rd
and fifth lines of Andrews code

Anyway, hope that helps...

	Message #2274 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

=?iso-8859-1?Q?Re:=A0ASCII?= Reader

Sun Jan 17, 1999 7:21 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 16-Jan-99, r!K wrote:
> #f$=fsel$("blahblah"..)#
> #If Exist(f$)#
> # Open In 1,f$ : SIZE=Lof(1)#
> # Reserve As Data 1,SIZE#
> # Bload 1,f$#
> #end if#

Don't use bank 1! It's for sprites! Use something like 10 instead.

> But I can't figure out how to display the thing on the screen.
> I suspect it may be Loke,Doke,Peek,Poke etc but I have no clue how to use
> them.......

ADR=Start(10)
Repeat
a$=Peek$(ADR,Chr$(10))
Add ADR,Len(a$) : Rem +1?
Print a$
Until ADR>Start(10)+Length(10)

That should be enough.

	Message #2282 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Finding attributes

Sun Jan 17, 1999 11:33 pm
"Chris Coulson" <chris@bay13.demon.co.uk>


> From: Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>

> (eg, for your locate example: P=Point(80,80) would give the paper
> colour anyway).

Assuming the character (if there is one) printed at that location
didn`t overwrite that particular pixel...

There isn`t any method I can think of that will reliably return the
pen and paper colours for a given character location, because even if
you scan the entire rectangle that the character requires, and find
out which two colours are present, you still wouldn`t know which
colour was pen and which was paper. I suppose you could do a spot of
OCR to determine what the character was, then figure out which pixels
it`d be drawn into, and match the colours accordingly, but you`re
talking a LOT of work.

Probably the easiest and most reliable way to do it is to keep a
record of the pen/paper colours for each character location as you
print to that location, and read the values from this record rather
than trying to pull them directly from the screen. But that only
works if the screen in question has been rendered by your own code...


Chris

--
                          At Home With the Chris
         Amigas, Babylon 5, Flight Sims, RIAT'97-98 and Melanie C
                       http://www.tornado.pair.com/

On 18-Jan-99, Rune J. Keller wrote:
>How do I load a picture onto a GUI screen?

I use the paste bob command. Write a simple amos prg to load your pic and save
it into a bob, then paste it into your new location. Of course, it will only
work with ecs screens (but you can do 32 colour hi res with a bit of juggling)

"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>



GB> Sure. Just read the hardware port with a Peek (or was it a Deek).
LM> I've ALLWAYS wanted to know this.... how the hell do you know where
LM> to peek poke deek doke leek and loke things? I knows they are
LM> memory addresses but how do you find out which are which?

Well, there is no way to determine something like that without getting
your hands on the proper documentation... I suppose you could write
a program that looped through every memory address and monitored
the value at each location for a few seconds while you moved the
joystick but that would certainly take a LONG time just to find the
location of that one port address. I have done things like that but I
would not recommend it... hahahaha. :)

I have Compute's Mapping the Amiga which is documents all of these
hardware addresses... also have Abacus's "Amiga Graphics Inside &
Out" which documents a bunch of other stuff.

There is a hardware manual free for download but I cannot remember
what it is called now... it is in Amiga Guide form. Check Aminet
under the "Dev/" drawer for the Amiga Hardware Manual (???). :-)

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2300 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Hardware Addresses...

Mon Jan 18, 1999 7:05 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


LM> I've ALLWAYS wanted to know this.... how the hell do you know where
LM> to peek poke deek doke leek and loke things? I knows they are
LM> memory addresses but how do you find out which are which?
GB> Well, there is no way to determine something like that without
GB> getting your hands on the proper documentation...

...and with that being said here is some documentation:

The JOY1DAT ($DFF00C) register = joystick port 2
If (JOY1DAT And 512) Then Joystick is pushed Left
If (JOY1DAT And 2) Then Joystick is pushed Right
Up and Down are left as an exercise for the reader. :-)

The CIA-A PRA ($BFE001) register = left button for both ports
Bit 6 returns the status of the left button for the Mouse Port
Bit 7 returns the status of the left button for the Joy Port

The POTGOR ($DFF016) register = right button for both ports
Bit 10 returns the status of the right button for the Mouse Port
Bit 14 returns the status of the right button for the Joy Port

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

Re: Control WB via AMOS (putting it lightly)

Mon Jan 18, 1999 7:01 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


-----Original Message-----
From: Lee Marchment <Lee@rgb-bbs.freeserve.co.uk>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 17 January 1999 12:31
Subject: [amos-list] Control WB via AMOS (putting it lightly)


>From: Lee Marchment <Lee@rgb-bbs.freeserve.co.uk>
>
>Hiya!
>You know when you go to the white bar at the top of yer Workbench screen
and
>click on it and you can drag it to reveal sreens under it?? will i was
>wondering if any one out there knew if there was anyway of controling where
>the workbench screen sits via AMOS???
>I would have thought it would probally use peeks and pokes most likely
>Thanks!

Here! I was wrong the doking code didn't work so instead here is an intcall!
' Grab the WB Handle
S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
S=Intcall(-510)
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
Areg(1)=0
NULL=Intcall(-516)

' The Screen Handle
Areg(0)=WBHAN
' The X Increment
Dreg(0)=X
' The Y increment
Dreg(1)=Y
' The call!
NULL=Intcall(-162)


I hope its what you want!
Phil!

AMOS Development dead?

Mon Jan 18, 1999 8:21 pm
"Rev. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


December went by with nothing but air. The promised AMOS update never
materialized. Neither have any of the developers.

The official amos home pages have no new news since July 30, 1998. TGE had a
beta out Dec. 30, 1998 but the rumour mill says tge is deader than ibm
technology.

If you're looking for the AMOS update, you'll have to find someone who
actually lives near the developers and send them to pound on the door, because
none of them are answering email, either to this list or personal.

Personally, I'd love to see the AMOS updates. I've seen betas of tge and gui,
but, by now, the general public has caught up with the betatesters and nothing
new is forthcoming.

The developers are on this list, and most likely reading all the mail we send.
How about a response?

What is the status of the AMOS update?
What is the truth behind TGE?
What is happening with the GUI 2.0 release?
Why won't any of the developers talk to the people who support AMOS? Are they
practicing to be Amiga developers like so many others?
If you aren't talking to the people who will use the program, who are you
talking to?
Update the damn AMOS pages!

	Message #2315 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Control WB via AMOS

Mon Jan 18, 1999 9:59 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


LM> You know when you go to the white bar at the top of yer Workbench
LM> screen and click on it and you can drag it to reveal sreens under it??
LM> Well I was wondering if any one out there knew if there was anyway of
LM> controling where the workbench screen sits via AMOS???
PG> ...here is an intcall!
PG> ' Grab the WB Handle
PG> S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
PG> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
PG> S=Intcall(-510)
PG> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
PG> Areg(1)=0
PG> NULL=Intcall(-516)
PG> 'The Screen Handle
PG> Areg(0)=WBHAN
PG> ' The X Increment
PG> Dreg(0)=X
PG> ' The Y increment
PG> Dreg(1)=Y
PG> ' The call!
PG> NULL=Intcall(-162)

Okay... it is very nice of you to send this stuff but I am sure that
to anybody who is interested in learning the OS, this looks VERY
cryptic. Can I convince you to add a little documentation to future
posts? :)

Also, this code will fail as you are loading A0 with an unintialized
variable (WBHAN)... below is modified code...
----------------------------------
' OS Library Vector (Function) Offsets...
LVO_LOCK_PUB_SCREEN = -510
LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN = -516
LVO_MOVE_SCREEN = -162

Rem We need to obtain the Screen Pointer for WorkBench
Rem because the Move_Screen library function requires it...
' So, we build a NULL-terminated string containing the name...
S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
' Then we load the address of this string into Register A0...
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
' Now, we Lock "Workbench" and receive the Screen Pointer...
WBHANDLE=Intcall( LVO_LOCK_PUB_SCREEN )

Rem Now, we can Unlock Workbench (just means that the screen
Rem can now be closed). Actually, this would be better after the
Rem Move_Screen code but I kept it here for consistency...
' Again, we load the address of this string into Register A0...
Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
' We also need the Screen Pointer...
Areg(1)=WBHANDLE
' Now, we Unlock "Workbench"...
Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )

Some quick notes: You only need to supply either the Name or
Screen pointer.
If you give the name in A0 then you can simply use 0 in A1
If you give the Screen Pointer in A1 then you can use 0 in A0
I used both but WBHANDLE will simply be ignored.

Rem Finally, now that we have our obtained our Screen
Rem Handle we can actually move the Workbench screen...
' Pointer to the Workbench Screen (WB Screen Handle)...
Areg(0)=WBHANDLE
' The X OFFSET is ignored but we supply it anyway (use 0)...
Dreg(0)=XOFFSET
' Set YOFFSET= to the vertical position you desire...
Dreg(1)=YOFFSET
' The perform the Screen Move...
Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN )

Okay, I do not mean to target you Phil (PHIL GLANVILLE) but the
Amiga OS can seem quite complex and most of the time I think
this is due to the fact that people do not document their code.
With a bit of documentation things become so much clearer!! :-)

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2321 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Control WB via AMOS

Tue Jan 19, 1999 1:30 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


Okay, I have discovered that AMOS requires you to receive a
value from the library calls even if they do not return anything. :)

So, in these lines...
> ' Now, we Unlock "Workbench"...
> Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
> ' The perform the Screen Move...
> Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN )

Add a "VOID=" in front of the two Intcall statements like so...
VOID=Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
VOID=Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN)

This way we can easily see we are to consider that no value is returned.
Which I imagine is the reason Phil was using "NULL=". :-) Hahahaha.


Also note that XOFFSET and YOFFSET are delta values, not absolute
screen position values. This means that YOFFSET=-1 moves up by one
pixel while YOFFSET=2 moves down by two pixels, and so on.

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

Re: LightWave Addon...

Tue Jan 19, 1999 12:02 pm
"Keith Hill" <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


>ST> I wanted a small util to sit in the background and monitor LW's
>ST> arexx port, and (using speech) say things like...
>ST> "Frame 72 finished rendering"
>ST> "Frame 72 took 8mins 34seconds"
>ST> "Frame 73 rendering"
> Cool... I really like this idea!! Kind of like Star Trek technology.
> Hahahaha. Should be possible to create an Amos program that
> can somehow monitor that... but I am not familiar with Arexx port
> communication. Hahahaha. :-)
> I am almost positive that I have read messages on this list from people
> who have already experimented with this type of Arexx communication
> via AMOS programming. I know some of you people have... maybe it
> was Giark or Keith??


It was Giark who was into arexx, but there is another way to do the
lightwave thing, but it won;t do everything you want. Monitor the render
directory for changes, and then announce that. Yeah, it's not as pretty,
but you'll have a heck of a lot more success, and it'll be a LOT easier than
trying to monitor another proggie that may or may not be outputting the
right signals.

The thing you need to do if you are with hte arexx thingie, is to find what
port lightwave is using to tell whats going on, and then pretend to be a
toaster or something.

Yeah, I know it doesn't help much.

Have fun NEway.

-----Original Message-----
From: Garfield Benjamin <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 18 January 1999 21:41
Subject: [amos-list] Re: Control WB via AMOS


>From: "Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>
>
>LM> You know when you go to the white bar at the top of yer Workbench
>LM> screen and click on it and you can drag it to reveal sreens under it??
>LM> Well I was wondering if any one out there knew if there was anyway of
>LM> controling where the workbench screen sits via AMOS???
> PG> ...here is an intcall!
> PG> ' Grab the WB Handle
> PG> S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
> PG> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
> PG> S=Intcall(-510)
> PG> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
> PG> Areg(1)=0
> PG> NULL=Intcall(-516)
> PG> 'The Screen Handle
> PG> Areg(0)=WBHAN
> PG> ' The X Increment
> PG> Dreg(0)=X
> PG> ' The Y increment
> PG> Dreg(1)=Y
> PG> ' The call!
> PG> NULL=Intcall(-162)
>
> Okay... it is very nice of you to send this stuff but I am sure that
> to anybody who is interested in learning the OS, this looks VERY
> cryptic. Can I convince you to add a little documentation to future
> posts? :)
>
> Also, this code will fail as you are loading A0 with an unintialized
> variable (WBHAN)... below is modified code...
>----------------------------------
> ' OS Library Vector (Function) Offsets...
> LVO_LOCK_PUB_SCREEN = -510
> LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN = -516
> LVO_MOVE_SCREEN = -162
>
> Rem We need to obtain the Screen Pointer for WorkBench
> Rem because the Move_Screen library function requires it...
> ' So, we build a NULL-terminated string containing the name...
> S$="Workbench"+Chr$(0)
> ' Then we load the address of this string into Register A0...
> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
> ' Now, we Lock "Workbench" and receive the Screen Pointer...
> WBHANDLE=Intcall( LVO_LOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
>
> Rem Now, we can Unlock Workbench (just means that the screen
> Rem can now be closed). Actually, this would be better after the
> Rem Move_Screen code but I kept it here for consistency...
> ' Again, we load the address of this string into Register A0...
> Areg(0)=Varptr(S$)
> ' We also need the Screen Pointer...
> Areg(1)=WBHANDLE
> ' Now, we Unlock "Workbench"...
> Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
>

erm no Intcall output!

> Some quick notes: You only need to supply either the Name or
> Screen pointer.
> If you give the name in A0 then you can simply use 0 in A1
> If you give the Screen Pointer in A1 then you can use 0 in A0
> I used both but WBHANDLE will simply be ignored.
>
> Rem Finally, now that we have our obtained our Screen
> Rem Handle we can actually move the Workbench screen...
> ' Pointer to the Workbench Screen (WB Screen Handle)...
> Areg(0)=WBHANDLE

I know i noticed the error after send it... as you will see from the
emails... i just ripped this from some of my code. i changed most of the
stuff except that!

> ' The X OFFSET is ignored but we supply it anyway (use 0)...
> Dreg(0)=XOFFSET
> ' Set YOFFSET= to the vertical position you desire...
> Dreg(1)=YOFFSET
> ' The perform the Screen Move...
> Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN )
>

and again!

> Okay, I do not mean to target you Phil (PHIL GLANVILLE) but the

>From: "Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>
>
>Okay, I have discovered that AMOS requires you to receive a
>value from the library calls even if they do not return anything. :)
>
>So, in these lines...
>> ' Now, we Unlock "Workbench"...
>> Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
>> ' The perform the Screen Move...
>> Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN )
>
>Add a "VOID=" in front of the two Intcall statements like so...
> VOID=Intcall( LVO_UNLOCK_PUB_SCREEN )
> VOID=Intcall( LVO_MOVE_SCREEN)
>

Aha! You spotted it!

>This way we can easily see we are to consider that no value is returned.
>Which I imagine is the reason Phil was using "NULL=". :-) Hahahaha.

okay you're mad!

Hehehe!!!! =O)

>
>
>Also note that XOFFSET and YOFFSET are delta values, not absolute
>screen position values. This means that YOFFSET=-1 moves up by one
>pixel while YOFFSET=2 moves down by two pixels, and so on.


yep! thats why they are called offsets!

=O)

Re: LightWave Addon...

Tue Jan 19, 1999 4:40 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


ST> I wanted a small util to sit in the background and monitor LW's
ST> arexx port, and (using speech) say things like...
ST> "Frame 72 finished rendering"
ST> "Frame 72 took 8mins 34seconds"
ST> "Frame 73 rendering"
KH> It was Giark who was into arexx, but there is another way to do the
KH> lightwave thing, but it won;t do everything you want. Monitor the
KH> render directory for changes, and then announce that. Yeah, it's not
KH> as pretty, but you'll have a heck of a lot more success, and it'll be
KH> a LOT easier than trying to monitor another proggie that may or may
KH> not be outputting the right signals.

Actually, a cool idea! Shows what every good programmer soon
learns... there is always more than one way to do something. Arexx
might be the "proper" way but many times we just need to use the way
that we can implement in the least amount of time, etc.

This actually sounds like a cool project as the resulting "technology"
could be useful for future projects. :-)

"David Vivash" <PMA98DAV@sheffield.ac.uk>


> From: "Rev. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>
>
> On 19-Jan-99, David Vivash wrote:
> >Has anyone on this list managed to get AMOS working under UAE?
>
> I haven't tried yet, but it seems simple enough.
>
> >to get an Amiga disk image of AMOS (at 880k) onto a disk to transfer
>
> Why? No one says you have to keep the disk structure. Copy as many files as
> you can (PC0:) and put them on the ibm uae partition, then copy the rest. AMOS
> disks aren't a special format or anything.

Yeah but to get a disk working in UAE you have to have a disk image
of the disk (an .adf file). The version of UAE I have has four slots
representing disk drives (Df0: - Df3:). You put the adf file in one
of those slots and the UAE thingy treats it as a disk.
Thats why I need to get .adf files of the AMOS disks. But, as I said
before these files are as big as an Amiga disk and wont fit on my PC
formatted disks.

I wouldn't have this problem if PC's used decent disk formats.

Anyway, I'll keep working at it...

David

too,
the way I got a disk image is to use Transadf which is on Aminet to make the
disk image

need to split the resulting image file into smaller files that will fit
onto a 720k pc disk.

Use Sploin for this purpose also available on Aminet.

Re: LightWave Addon...

Wed Jan 20, 1999 3:20 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


ST> I wanted a small util to sit in the background and monitor LW's
KH> there is another way to do the lightwave thing... Monitor the render
KH> directory for changes, and then announce that.
GB> This actually sounds like a cool project as the resulting
GB> "technology" could be useful for future projects. :-)

Well, you had to know from that last comment that I was going to
have a shot at this, right? Hahahaha. :)
Anyway, I had a few free hours this evening so I worked on this
project. At the moment it asks you for the Directory to monitor,
the duration of "The Watch", and the frequency of the Directory
Scans during this time.
If you select a 60 second Monitor Duration and Lowest Frequency of
1, the DirectoryMonitor will scan for changes once during this 60
second period. If you select the Highest Frequency of 100 the DM
will scan the Directory for changes 100 times during this 60 second
period... well, theoretically that is how it works but I have made
it so waits at least 6 seconds between scans as I see no need in
bogging down the drive.
The File Info lists are dynamically allocated and the speed is not
too bad on my 10MB 14MHz A1200 system. I can scan the entire C/
folder (240 files) on my hard drive (creating the file list) in
about 4 seconds. After that the scans for modification take around
2.5 seconds and of course all of this will be faster on higher
processors!!

So, in the end what do we have at this point? Not much! :)
I can tell it what drawer to watch, how long to watch, and how
often to check... then I can copy some files over to that drawer or
delete some files and the Directory Monitor (in the background)
will respond with something like...
>>> Scan #4...
3 File(s) Created
or if I delete some then it will be something like...
>>> Scan #7...
2 File(s) Deleted

Okay, as far as monitoring the LW rendering directory... the
problem I foresee it is that if LW renders to disk (rather than to
mem then copying to disk) the file will be "Created" as soon as
LW opens it... now it will be open for as long as LW is rendering.
The problem is how to detect when the file is done. I have come
up with two options at this point...
1. As soon as another file Creation is detected... record that
Start Time and also use that as the End Time for the last
file, giving a rough idea of the Elapsed Time.
2. once a file Creation has been detected... stop scanning the
directory and instead attempt to Monitor the file size of
the newly created file. Once a certain amount of time has
elapsed and the file size remains constant then we can
assume the file is complete.

This has been a a fun project to work on and I think it will
turn out pretty good when complete. I do not have any more
time tonight but that will give the rest of you guys something
to think about. I welcome all suggestions. :-)

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

GB> Okay, as far as monitoring the LW rendering directory... the
GB> problem I foresee is that if LW renders to disk (rather than to mem
ST> Actually LW doesn't save the pic until its finished rendering, unlike
ST> Imagine, which saves every scanline...

Cool... makes it much simpler. I do not have Lightwave so any
info you can provide will help. Just knowing that it copies the
picture to disk "all at once" is a big help in selecting the right
design to "catch" the files as they are created. Thanks. :-)


GB> This has been a a fun project to work on and I think it will
GB> turn out pretty good when complete. I do not have any more
GB> time tonight but that will give the rest of you guys something
GB> to think about. I welcome all suggestions. :-)
ST> Well, when its finishd send it to me... bwahahahaha

Of course, that is my intention!! This was your idea after all. :-)

Currently, I am simply creating a general purpose Directory
Monitor utility... which will give us a solid foundation. Like I
said, at this point you can launch it from Workbench, answer
a few questions then it "hides" and monitors. If you copy some
files into the directory being monitored then the DirectoryMonitor
will inform you with a very generic output of something like...
Scan# 10
>>> 3 Files Were Created.
Attempting To Identify Files...
>>> File "Atest1" was created.
>>> File "Atest2" was created.
>>> File "Atest3" was created.
Same output style for detection of Deleted/Removed Files.

Should not take long to create your specialized version, a day
or two at most providing I can spare a few hours in the evenings.

Also, working on this project has allowed me to see that it would
be SIMPLE to create a Find utility which is something I really miss
when I am working on the Amiga Workbench!! Plan to throw one
of them together after your LWM program is done.

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com
