	Message #2377 of 8249 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: LightWave Addon...

Thu Jan 21, 1999 3:27 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


GB> Just knowing that it copies the picture to disk "all at once" is a
GB> big help in selecting the right design to "catch" the files as they
GB> are created. Thanks. :-)
ST> I'd like to know how you'll work out how long the render took ;)

Well, what I am thinking at the moment is...
1. Once the DM is first launched and performs the first scan of the
directory (building the data tables) it will then record the time.
2. Now, the DM will monitor until a new file appears.
The time is now recorded and the former time is subtracted which
will give a very rough approximation of the true elapsed time.
Properly timing this FIRST frame is the hardest because we have
no real point of reference. However, as soon as a file has been
created we will have our point of reference and be able to more
accurately guage the time.

That's the general idea at the moment.. how well it will work in
practice in another thing entirely. :) Hahahaha.


GB> Currently, I am simply creating a general purpose Directory
GB> Monitor...
ST> If this util is constantly monitoring the dir, won't it eat up many
ST> cpu cycles..? after all I only have a PPC 060/50 and not an
ST> 800mhz monster ;)

Hahahaha... I had this same concern so the DM will not scan the
directory more frequently than 10 times per minute and is actually
user selectable so you can make scan only 5 times per minute.
On my 14 MHz 68020 I can scan a directory containing 240 files in
2.5 seconds... I can scan the RAM Disk in something like 0.25
seconds!!! So, render to RAM: if at all possible. ;-)


GB> Should not take long to create your specialized version, a day
GB> or two at most providing I can spare a few hours in the evenings.
ST> Wow, you are good.. heh, it took me 2 days of playing with amos,
ST> just to get a gui window open... ;) hehehe I'm a lame coder :)

Too true... I am GOOD but my most redeeming quality is the fact
that I am so humble!! Hahahaha. :-)
Just experiment and have fun with the Amos programming... that is
the fastest way to learn. This Directory Monitor project isn't
something anyone would consider a Beginner's Project!!! Hahaha.


GB> ...it would be SIMPLE to create a Find utility which is something I
GB> really miss when I am working on the Amiga Workbench!!
ST> why not just use "file locator" its small and very good, Its PD
ST> so I'll be happy to send you it if you want.?

Hahaha... yeah that could work too! :)
Sure, send it to my personal email address below. :-)

WAIT!! The light bulb has come on.. imagine that?! Hahahaha.

When LightWave renders these files how does it name them?
Suppose I entered "TestRender" for the name of a set of 20
renderings... would LightWave simply create the files like this?
"TestRender01"
"TestRender02"
.........................
"TestRender20"

If so then we can greatly simply this whole thing. All we need to
do is generate the file name then use Exist(FileName) to check
for its creation... no need to scan the entire directory dynamically
building the file lists!!!!

Let me know if this is how LightWave does it. :-)

extensions

Thu Jan 21, 1999 4:01 pm
Ken <cbminfo@digital.net>


Can someone explain step by step just how to get an extension working and a
program readily available from aminet maybe that uses extensions ?

ie: tried installing the amcaf files yesterday, even went so far as to run the

installer. It finally said done, said I'd get a requestor (never happened)
using a file from the demo, it said unknown extension.

Here's a portion of examine.amos from the amcaf examples directory.

' Create a nice looking palette.
Palette 0,$FFF
' Open a file selector, where you can choose a file to be examined.
FILE$=Fsel$("","","Select a file!","")
' Has the user clicked on Cancel?
If FILE$="" Then End
' Examine the object. Then jump to a output routine.
Extension I FILE$
Gosub OUTPUT
' Wait for keypress.

Can someone tell me what extension I is ?

installed - in this case I assume that to be amcaf. Check the docs
about installation and try to install it again...

Re: LightWave Addon...

Stephen Thornber <SThornber@steve1.demon.co.uk>



Hi Garfield

GB> Well, what I am thinking at the moment is...
GB> 1. Once the DM is first launched and performs the first scan of the
GB> directory (building the data tables) it will then record the time.
GB> 2. Now, the DM will monitor until a new file appears.
GB> The time is now recorded and the former time is subtracted which
GB> will give a very rough approximation of the true elapsed time.
GB> Properly timing this FIRST frame is the hardest because we have
GB> no real point of reference. However, as soon as a file has been
GB> created we will have our point of reference and be able to more
GB> accurately guage the time.
GB> That's the general idea at the moment.. how well it will work in
GB> practice in another thing entirely. :) Hahahaha.

	Message #2397 of 8249

Re: Grabbing AMOS Screens

Fri Jan 22, 1999 3:00 am
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 21-Jan-99, Rune J. Keller wrote:
>
> On 21-Jan-99, Andy "Mushroom" Kellett wrote:
>
>> Can anyone reccomend a decent screengrab program that will grab AMOS
>> screens, even from AMOS compiled programs?
>
> I have never heard of a program than can accomplice this task. My own
> AmosGrab can grab an Amos screen in a tricky way, but only if it is
> inserted in the code. I believe that is the only option you've got. Unless
> you have access to an Action Replay, which can probably do the job.

The underlying problem is that AMOS doesn't use the standard
structures (viewports, etc) that most other programs use. Since
the registers which actually control the display are write-only
there is no real way to obtain from the hardware exactly what
is going out, so you need to be able to read a copy from whatever
wrote it in the first place. Since AMOS's structures are quite
different, none of the normal grabbing techniques work. You
could chase down the screen table, or the copper lists, and try
to put it all together, but that is an ugly job.

One alternative pops to mind. Run the program under UAE, and
grab its screen?

Good luck,
-Richard

Back in good old A500/KS1.3 days there were at least one program which
viewed whole chipmem-area on a screen. At the same time you could change
bitplane depths, pointers and modulos. It also searched every copper
color-setting instruction from a memory to set correct colors. It wasn't as
easy to use as ordinary screen grabbers but with it you could grab all
graphics f.ex. from Lotus and Desert Strike. It worked fine with amos'
screens. After I got KS2.04 it never worked properly anymore. I can't
really remember its name but there should be same kind of tools for newer
kickstarts and chipsets. At least AdEd.lha in the Aminet should allow you
to do some memory scanning (says readme-file not me;P).

Hi there

As said...

> Has anyone on this list managed to get AMOS working under UAE?
> I was going to give it a go but I got stuck at the first hurdle - how
> to get an Amiga disk image of AMOS (at 880k) onto a disk to transfer
> over to my PC (Double Density PC disk being 770K or whatever). If I
> do eventually find a way, does anyone know how well AMOS works under
> UAE? ...(if it works at all)

First , set up a HD (drawer) on your uae(pc) and install workbench
and lha
then , just use PC0 to copy lha archived stuff (can be amos) to pc
disks and move the archive direct to your HD (drawer) , after so ,
when booting uae you just unarchive the stuff.
This can be hard to set up but it gets efficient later on
Amos works weirdly on uae , some things don't work at all
in my really personal opinion , it totaly sucks and don't even
bother speed.

Hope it helps ,

	Message #2407 of 8250

Re: Grabbing AMOS Screens

Fri Jan 22, 1999 10:11 pm
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 22-Jan-99, Garfield Benjamin wrote:

>> Can anyone reccomend a decent screengrab program that will grab
>> AMOS screens, even from AMOS compiled programs?
>> I have never heard of a program than can accomplice this task.
> RG>The underlying problem is that AMOS doesn't use the standard
> RG>structures (viewports, etc) that most other programs use.
>
> I have often heard this but how exactly does AMOS do it? Doesn't
> it ultimately have to integrate its screens into the OS screen
> list?? I mean, if you traveled this linked-list by following the
> *NextScreen pointer wouldn't you eventually locate the AMOS
> screen(s)???

Well, no, actually. AMOS works its 'magic' by basically shutting
off most of the OS's control (including the Intuition screen list)
while it is in control. It swaps in its own copper list when it
is 'to Front' and restores normal function when it is 'to Back'.
This is the primary reason for most of its shortcommings (OS wise)
like not working on graphics cards or non-15KHz monitors and not
multitasking with itself. It does open a intuition screen and a
window, but those are not where the real action is.

There is a table of screens in the amos datazone, and one could
process it to make a reasonable map of what is on the display.
Something like this is found in equ.s (with a bar or underscore
in front for some versions) which is part of the extention sources
that were bundled with most amoses (How does one pluralize AMOS?)

('Ec' is for Ecrans, which seems to be french for screens. The
comments to the right are mine, so they may be wrong, BTW)

--
RsReset
* Bitmap address
EcLogic: rs.l 6
EcPhysic rs.l 6
EcCurrent: rs.l 6 ; current bitplane pointers

* Datas!
EcCon0: rs.w 1 ; BPLCON0
EcCon2: rs.w 1 ; BPLCON2
EcTx: rs.w 1
EcTy: rs.w 1
EcNPlan: rs.w 1
EcWX: rs.w 1
EcWY: rs.w 1
EcWTx: rs.w 1
EcWTy: rs.w 1
EcVX: rs.w 1
EcVY: rs.w 1

EcDEcran: rs.l 1
EcColorMap rs.w 1
EcNbCol rs.w 1
EcPal rs.w 32 ; color values
..
<LOTS of stuff snipped here>
...

; Length of a screen
EcLong: equ __RS

--

Anyway, that defines the structure of an amos screen. There is a
table of these pointed to by 'Screen Base', which means each
screen will be offset by 'EcLong' past screen base, IIRC. There
is enough there to build an image of most of what is on display,
but the program to do it would be almost as complicated as the
custom chips to do it for ALL cases. (BTW, hardware sprites,
copper effects, rainbows and other such things would not be in
this list, and remember, multiple resolution screens can be
intermixed, so things could get tricky.

Hope this rather lenghty post is at least interesting to some,
-Richard

P.S. Anyone else enjoying (or being frustrated by) the clickteam
source release?


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #2408 of 8250

Re: Grabbing AMOS Screens

Fri Jan 22, 1999 11:49 pm
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 22-Jan-99, Richard Griffith wrote:

...
> table of these pointed to by 'Screen Base', which means each
> screen will be offset by 'EcLong' past screen base, IIRC. There

What a moron, spewing garbage and replying to his own post!

Actually, just a small correction. Screen Base returns the
address for the active screen only. There is a table of addresses
to the 'screen base' for each numbered screen, but amos does not
seem to give the address of the table. Sorry.

-Richard

	Message #2409 of 8250 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Grabbing AMOS Screens

Sat Jan 23, 1999 2:20 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


RG> Well, no, actually. AMOS works its 'magic' by basically shutting
RG> off most of the OS's control (including the Intuition screen list)
RG> while it is in control. It swaps in its own copper list when it
RG> is 'to Front' and restores normal function when it is 'to Back'.
RG> This is the primary reason for most of its shortcommings (OS wise)
RG> like not working on graphics cards or non-15KHz monitors and not
RG> multitasking with itself. It does open a intuition screen and a
RG> window, but those are not where the real action is.

Okay, I gotcha. Instead of utilizing a normal Intuition Screen and
Window, Amos is going to the next level which is to simply generate
a Display. This is the same approach used by BLITZ when in Blitz
mode. Actually, this is kind of an easier way to handle things as they
can focus on just the Display without getting bogged down in all the
other stuff. :)


RG> Hope this rather lenghty post is at least interesting to some,

Sure... at least now we have a better understanding of just how
Amos is stucturing everything. :-)

Garfield Benjamin    e-mail: gbenjam@sosbbs.com

	Message #2415 of 8250 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Mouse pointer collision

Sat Jan 23, 1999 11:13 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> On 23-Jan-99, r!K wrote:
>> What I want to do is to recognise when the pointer collides with
(moves
>> over) these BOBS.

> Are the bobs stationary? If so, set up zones around them. If not, use
x mouse
> and y mouse to check if the pointer is over the bob positions.

Nah, you dont want to do that.

The problem is that, although the mouse pointer is a sprite, its not
created by the amos program exactly.

The way to do it is to hide the mouse pointer and then do

"Sprite 1,x mouse,y mouse,1" every vbl

This'll create a sprite where the pointer would be and then
Bob-sprite collision'll work fine

See ya.
--

	Message #2426 of 8250

Re: Mouse pointer collision

Mon Jan 25, 1999 1:05 am
Andy H <geosync@space.net.au>


Hi,

> > yes but depending on how fast the program will be running, the fake
> mouse
> > pointer (sprite) would jerk and not follow the mouse position
> correctly, as

If you make the sprite using AMAL it updates as quickly as the mouse
pointer. It`s in the manual on how to do this. Here`s an extract....

Inside Autotest
Here's the previous example rewritten using the Autotest feature.

Load "AMOS_DATA:Sprites/octopus.abk'
Sprite 8,130,50,1: Get Sprite Palette
A$="AUtotest (If R0<>XM Jump Update"
A$=A$+"If R1<>YM Jump Update else eXit"
A$=A$+"Update: Let R0=XM; Let R1=YM; Direct M)": Rem End of autotest
A$=A$+'M: Move R0-X,RI-Y,20 Wait;": Rem Try changing 20 to different
valuesl
Amal 8,A$: Amal on

The sprite now smoothly follows your mouse, no matter how fast you move
it. The action of this program is as follows:
Every 50th of a second the mouse coordinates are tested using the XM and
YM functions. If they are unchanged since the last test, the Autotest is
aborted using the exit command. The main program now resumes precisely
where it left off.
However if the mouse has been moved, the autotest routine will restart
the main program again from the beginning (label M) using the new
coordinates in XM and YM respectively.

Hope this is helpful.
Andy H.

	Message #2430 of 8250

Re: setting bits of a variable

Mon Jan 25, 1999 7:11 am
<Magnus.Sjoberg@asdo.se>


> Cori Skagen <lskagen@ssm.ca> wrote:
>
>I was just wondering is there an easy way of setting a series of
bits
>in a variable?

>I know the btst comand but that only sets one bit at a time, I want
>to set a series of bits..

>I could AND them with zero and then OR them with the new value, but
is there
>an easier way?

You don't need to AND them with zero first.

If you gonna set one (or more) bits, OR the variable with the bit(s)
like:
10010011 OR 101 => 10010111

And if you want to clear one bit, AND the variable with all bits
exept
the ones you want to clear.
10010111 AND 11111011 => 10010011

Magnus

If at first you don't succeed, skydiving is not for you.

	Message #2434 of 8250 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Slider Gadgets and Preset Values

Mon Jan 25, 1999 4:05 pm
"Rev. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


On 25-Jan-99, Declan Gorman wrote:
> My problem is that I cannot display decimal numbers as they seem to be
>rounded off to the nearest whole number. ie. "0.5" is displayed as "1".

I found the same problem. It is in the GUI extension and Pietro seems to have
died. The only solution is to make a text gadget and use the str$() function
to change your number into a string.

A$=Str$(YOURNUM#)
'Remember that you must use the # after variables if they are floating point,
or AMOS will chop the decimals off itself
Gui Set 1,1,0,Varptr(A$)

	Message #2456 of 8250

Re: Fonts

Tue Jan 26, 1999 12:13 pm
"Ives, Neil, IVESNJ" <neil.ives@bt.com>


> Does anyone know how to avoid scanning the entire Fonts: dir for fonts
(Get
> Fonts) when you just want to grab one font?

I think you can put the required fonts in the program directory and assign
the path to them before Amos looks for them. Dont forget to re-assign to
your system fonts before quiting Amos though.

Neil Ives
